  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_f6a83c4e-3ad9-42f3-bb29-36631651f536'
      });
    }

      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };

<div class='allCommunityAnswers'>
<div class='communityAnswer'>
<div class='communityAnswerBody'>
<div class='answererUserIcon'>
<a class="leftAlignedImage userPhoto" href="/user/show/82348831-hazel"><img alt="" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/users/1527880899i/82348831._UY100_CR16,0,100,100_.jpg" /></a>

<div class='communityAnswerTextContainer'>
<span class='communityAnswererName'>
<a href="/user/show/82348831-hazel">Hazel</a>
</span>
<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<div class='spoiler'>
This answer contains spoilers…
<span class='spoilerAnswerText'>
<a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[
  
    Through the third series, Power of Three, it is believed that Lionblaze, Jayfeather, and Hollyleaf are Squirrelflight and Brambleclaw's kits. However,<a href="#" rel="nofollow noopener">…more</a>
    Through the third series, Power of Three, it is believed that Lionblaze, Jayfeather, and Hollyleaf are Squirrelflight and Brambleclaw's kits. However, it turns out that they are actually the kits of Leafpool and Crowfeather, Crowfeather of which does not know that they are his children. Leafpool gives her kits to Squirrelflight to raise and keeps their true origins a secret from the Clan until Hollyleaf reveals the truth at a Gathering. Brambleclaw did not know about this.<br />Later, in A Vision of Shadows, Squirrelflight and Brambleclaw, Bramblestar then, have four kits: Alderheart, Sparkpelt, Dandelionkit, and Juniperkit. Both Juniperkit and Dandelionkit die when they are young, but Alderheart and Sparkpelt live on with Alderheart being the protagonist of A Vision of Shadows.<a href="#" rel="nofollow noopener">(less)</a>
  
 <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>
</span>
</div>
</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer10521887311430476381">This book is amazing. Every time I finish it, even if it's not for the first time, my heart beats as furiously, I am as sweaty and pale, and I feel as shocked as if I had been in the book and experienced the appalling turmoil that the main character had just been in.   <span id="freeText10521887311430476381" style="display:none">This book is amazing. Every time I finish it, even if it's not for the first time, my heart beats as furiously, I am as sweaty and pale, and I feel as shocked as if I had been in the book and experienced the appalling turmoil that the main character had just been in. Every time I re-read it, it is as exciting and terrifying as if I had read it for the first time, and all the same things happen to me. It's the end that is the best part. <br /><br />It is everything that makes the best books so good. It is full of cruel treachery and betrayal, heightening suspense, heart-stopping excitement, intriguing mystery, paling shock, and more the like. I think that if an author not as talented as Erin Hunter would have braved to write such an ending, it wouldn't have been as good. I think this is my favorite book in the whole warriors series. Even Erin Hunter would be hard-pushed to write a warriors book in a better way. <br /><br />After the badger attack, Squirrelflight and Brambleclaw push away their conflicts and come together. Squirrelflight trusts Brambleclaw fully again, but Leafpool isn't so sure. She knows Tigerstar still haunts Brambleclaw's dreams, and how loyal can Brambleclaw be with his father's temptations hanging over him? Meanwhile, Brambleclaw struggles to stay loyal to his Clan and not give in to the path of his father's footsteps... </span>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4845030-micheline?shelf=creature-characters">creature-characters</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4845030-micheline?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4845030-micheline?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4845030-micheline?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer159697253&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer159697253" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8842739247179653992">I was super anxious starting this book. As the last book of the New Prophecy series, I knew many questions would be answered, but I almost didnt want to know which way things were going to go. I was happy the book was told from BrambleClaw's perspective and hoped that would be an omen that with all the difficult choices and temptations he had to face wouldn't take him off his path. All throughout the book he keeps dreaming about his evil (and dead) father TigerStar, and joined bu his brother Haw</span>
  <span id="freeText8842739247179653992" style="display:none">I was super anxious starting this book. As the last book of the New Prophecy series, I knew many questions would be answered, but I almost didnt want to know which way things were going to go. I was happy the book was told from BrambleClaw's perspective and hoped that would be an omen that with all the difficult choices and temptations he had to face wouldn't take him off his path. All throughout the book he keeps dreaming about his evil (and dead) father TigerStar, and joined bu his brother HawkFrost, in the dreams, TigerStar coaches them on gaining power and leading all the 4 clans among both of them. It is clear that BrambleClaw has misgivings about some things his father says, and in his waking hours he is a loyal ThunderClan cat, but the meetings with his father, and his over ambitious brother had me feeling anxious. BrambleClaw is one of my favorite characters...<br /><br />The book's narration was shared again, by LeafPool, and she was also aware of BrambleClaw's dreams with TigerStar, and while she was often worried about this, she didnt let it could her judgment when StarClan gave her an omen that BrambleClaw was to be made clan deputy.<br /><br />I absolutely adored the whole New Prophecy series, although I felt this book ended a bit too abruptly for my taste. Once we finally know the outcome of the prophecy ''Before there is peace, blood will spill blood...'' the book comes to a close, without sharing anything more with the reader about the characters we've grown to care for all through the series. I knew the next series 'Warriors, Power of Three'' will probably show us more, but time will have passed and it will be from a new generation of cat's perspective. Seeing as I get way too emotionally invested in fictional characters, I will miss sharing BrambleClaw's thoughts, but I am very happy with this book as the final book of the New Prophecy! </span>
  <a data-text-id="8842739247179653992" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer1597383729" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1374711825330773633">Summary:<br/>Soon after the cats reached their new home by the lake, ThunderClan's medicine cat Leafpool received an ominous warning from StarClan: Before there is peace, blood will spill blood, and the lake will run red. As the Clan slowly recovers from a devastating badger attack, Leafpool can't help but wonder . . . do her prophetic dreams mean there are even worse dangers still in store for the warrior cats?<br/>At the same time, shadows of the past continue to haunt the forest as some old friends str</span>
  <span id="freeText1374711825330773633" style="display:none">Summary:<br />Soon after the cats reached their new home by the lake, ThunderClan's medicine cat Leafpool received an ominous warning from StarClan: Before there is peace, blood will spill blood, and the lake will run red. As the Clan slowly recovers from a devastating badger attack, Leafpool can't help but wonder . . . do her prophetic dreams mean there are even worse dangers still in store for the warrior cats?<br />At the same time, shadows of the past continue to haunt the forest as some old friends struggle to find their place, others appear to be lost forever, and an old enemy finds a new way to resurface in a quest for dark revenge. A sinister path is unfolding, and the time is coming for certain warriors to make the choices that will determine their destiny . . . and the destiny of all the Clans. <br />Plot:<br />I actually really loved the plot in this Warrior book. Of course, I always do. It was thrilling, and I read it in 1 day. In almost every Warrior book, there's a huge war, and I was glad to see a change for this one. There wasn't technically a war, but they was was major fights that were with few cats. Although, some plot twists were obvious, but yet again, Hunter leaves me off with a major cliffhanger and I MUST start the next book ASAP. <br />Writing:<br />Erin Hunter is my second favorite writer of all time. She/they are such amazing writers, and I LOVE their writing style. It's so easy to read, but it's beautifully complex at the same time. <br />Characters:<br />There was so much character development in this novel, it was unbelievable. Sometimes, you can't trust ANY cat, and you have to wait for the novel to reveal the traitor. One thing that bothered me, was Brambleclaw and Squirrelflight started picking up their "relationship" like nothing had EVER happened. That bothered me, and if you've read this book, you would know what I'm talking about. <br />Overall &amp; Recommendations:<br />This was such an amazing ending to The New Prophecy. I can't wait to start with The Power Of Three. Everything was perfect in this book, and barely anything bothered me. I would recommend starting the Warrior series in 5th grade. </span>

          </span>

<div id="review_2616006153" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2616006153" />
    <a title="HanjingW_C2" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/85620809-hanjingw-c2"><img alt="HanjingW_C2" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1548136178p2/85620809.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2616006153?book_show_action=true">Dec 06, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="HanjingW_C2" class="user" itemprop="url" name="HanjingW_C2" href="/user/show/85620809-hanjingw-c2">HanjingW_C2</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2616006153" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12110397932838565893">I've finished this book for the THIRD time, and it was as good as ever. This just proves that good books don't get boring. I think the theme I got was about the balance of kinship (blood relations like your cousin, relative, sibling etc) and justice. In the story, one of the main characters, Brambleclaw, was conflicted because his power-hungry father and half-brother would do anything to make him the leader of his clan. While Brambleclaw was loyal to his clan and the present leader, he also didn</span>
  <span id="freeText12110397932838565893" style="display:none">I've finished this book for the THIRD time, and it was as good as ever. This just proves that good books don't get boring. I think the theme I got was about the balance of kinship (blood relations like your cousin, relative, sibling etc) and justice. In the story, one of the main characters, Brambleclaw, was conflicted because his power-hungry father and half-brother would do anything to make him the leader of his clan. While Brambleclaw was loyal to his clan and the present leader, he also didn't want to disobey his father or lose his brother's trust. Throughout the book, I can see him struggling to compromise between these two conflicting ideas in his head. At the end of the story, Brambleclaw chose to save his clan and therefore kill his half-brother (his father was already dead and visited him in dreams), but he was still haunted because of that and was terrified that he spilled his kin's blood. I feel like the author is trying to tell us that it is normal to have conflicting thoughts. However, in the end, you should chose to do what you think is right, even if it means betraying your relatives. Traditional Chinese belief oppose that, and the Chinese culture tells us to stand behind our family no matter the circumstances. Overall, I think this concept is very interesting and deserve deeper thoughts. I think the ultimate question is: What is more important, family or justice? Do any of y'all have an opinion? Because I am very conflicted and would love to hear any thoughts. :)</span>
  <a data-text-id="12110397932838565893" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer14535331646485432240">Goodreads review of Warriors-The new prophecy: Sunset by Erin Hunter<br/>Review by: Naomi Willard<br/><br/>	Sunset is probably one of the more intense warriors books, showing the aftermath of the badger attack and what happens to ThunderClan afterwards and which clashes with other clans happen. After the badgers are fought off by ThunderClan, Stormfur and Brook Where Small Fish Swim journey to ThunderClan and arrive immediately after the last badger has left. (Besides Midnight) Shocked at what has happened, th</span>
  <span id="freeText14535331646485432240" style="display:none">Goodreads review of Warriors-The new prophecy: Sunset by Erin Hunter<br />Review by: Naomi Willard<br /><br />	Sunset is probably one of the more intense warriors books, showing the aftermath of the badger attack and what happens to ThunderClan afterwards and which clashes with other clans happen. After the badgers are fought off by ThunderClan, Stormfur and Brook Where Small Fish Swim journey to ThunderClan and arrive immediately after the last badger has left. (Besides Midnight) Shocked at what has happened, they offer to help rebuild the camp and help to return ThunderClan to full strength. Graystripe has been gone for moons and even Firestar is giving up hope. ThunderClan needs a new deputy, whether Graystripe is alive or not.<br />	I loved reading yet another of Erin Hunter’s masterpieces of a book and found myself tensing up at every battle and prophetic dream. I sort of wish that Firestar had waited longer for Graystripe to return because Graystripe is one of my favorite characters and it’s depressing when one of your favorite characters seems to be dead. (Hope you live Graystripe, we miss you.) I think Erin does a great job of describing every little detail, I felt almost like I WAS Brambleclaw at times, not just reading about him. I found it interesting to read about Leafpool especially, it’s cool to see what it’s like being a medicine cat. Overall, I loved this book! (Like pretty much every Warriors book ever.) <br /></span>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

<div id="review_3489688546" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3489688546" />
    <a title="Erin" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/90599773-erin"><img alt="Erin" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1544885601p2/90599773.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3489688546?book_show_action=true">Aug 15, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Erin" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Erin" href="/user/show/90599773-erin">Erin</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/90599773-erin?shelf=warrior-cats">warrior-cats</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/90599773-erin?shelf=owned">owned</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer3489688546&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3489688546" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5246715944160239761">This was one of the darkest, most suspenseful books in the series! There was so much going on here that worked well, tied up previous plotlines, and set the groundwork for future ones. The medicine cat storylines allowed a lot of previously hinted at issues to be solved here, from the sign about Mothwing to how Riverclan would receive messages from Starclan when Mothwing didn't believe in them. Leafpool really had the chance to shine here, which was a welcome change from her just spending time m</span>
  <span id="freeText5246715944160239761" style="display:none">This was one of the darkest, most suspenseful books in the series! There was so much going on here that worked well, tied up previous plotlines, and set the groundwork for future ones. The medicine cat storylines allowed a lot of previously hinted at issues to be solved here, from the sign about Mothwing to how Riverclan would receive messages from Starclan when Mothwing didn't believe in them. Leafpool really had the chance to shine here, which was a welcome change from her just spending time mooning over Crowfeather. Squirrelflight and Brambleclaw getting along so well was also a welcome change from the tension between them in the previous books. <br /><br />I always think my favorite group of cats was the original series ones, but this book in particular made me really love these second generation cats. So many of them got to have memorable, individual storylines; even cats that are considered background characters like Sorreltail, Cloudtail, Brightheart, and Rainwhisker.<br /><br />Out of everything this book set up for the next few books, I am most looking forward to seeing more of Cinderkit and seeing how the betrayal plotline unravels in the next series!</span>
  <a data-text-id="5246715944160239761" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3475891755" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13476031967195984574">Overall, this series as a whole is good, but I feel like there are several instances of rushing the plot or other developments in order to reach an easy resolution by the end of the series. I rather wish the series focused on just one cat's perspective, then maybe doing a deluxe edition from one or two of the other POVs that were featured throughout this series, ex. making this all from Brambleclaw's POV then giving Leafpool her own edition, or splitting it with Squirrelflight as well. I think s</span>
  <span id="freeText13476031967195984574" style="display:none">Overall, this series as a whole is good, but I feel like there are several instances of rushing the plot or other developments in order to reach an easy resolution by the end of the series. I rather wish the series focused on just one cat's perspective, then maybe doing a deluxe edition from one or two of the other POVs that were featured throughout this series, ex. making this all from Brambleclaw's POV then giving Leafpool her own edition, or splitting it with Squirrelflight as well. I think some of the drama and suspense is lost when we have different perspectives giving us all the information we need, rather than leaving us to dwell on it a little. But a solid series nonetheless.</span>

<div id="review_3030153214" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3030153214" />
    <a title="Historyprincess" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/12881308-historyprincess"><img alt="Historyprincess" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/u_50x66-632230dc9882b4352d753eedf9396530.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3030153214?book_show_action=true">Oct 31, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Historyprincess" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Historyprincess" href="/user/show/12881308-historyprincess">Historyprincess</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/30195775-sunset">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12881308-historyprincess?shelf=warriors">warriors</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer3030153214&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3030153214" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6280357442523376761">Premise: In the wake of a devastating attack, ThunderClan must confront their uncertain destiny. But no future of any individual cat is more shrouded in shadows than Brambleclaw's. For quite some time, the young tom has allowed a non-StarClan cat to walk in his dreams – and feed his near-consuming desire to be deputy of ThunderClan. But when he's forced to face the fact that he could be heading down a path far darker than he'd intended, Brambleclaw will ultimately have to decide how far he's wil</span>
  <span id="freeText6280357442523376761" style="display:none">Premise: In the wake of a devastating attack, ThunderClan must confront their uncertain destiny. But no future of any individual cat is more shrouded in shadows than Brambleclaw's. For quite some time, the young tom has allowed a non-StarClan cat to walk in his dreams – and feed his near-consuming desire to be deputy of ThunderClan. But when he's forced to face the fact that he could be heading down a path far darker than he'd intended, Brambleclaw will ultimately have to decide how far he's willing to go and how much he's willing to give up for power.<br /><br />Story/Writing: And so I'm finally done with the "New Prophecy" arc! It's always a little bittersweet to finish a book in this series, but it's even more so when I've come to the end of a fantastic arc such as this. It's not just as good as the "Prophecies Begin" arc. In some ways, it surpasses it. For one thing, I love how each of the titles for the books in this arc refer to something important in their respective stories. "Midnight" refers to Midnight the badger; "Moonrise" refers to the time when Stoneteller has a reading in the Cave of Pointed Stones; "Dawn" refers both to the time of day when the Clans begin their journey to the lake and to the dawn of a new era in their history; "Starlight" refers to the starlit stream Leafpool follows to discover the Moonpool; "Twilight" refers to the twilight of Cinderpelt's life; and "Sunset" obviously refers to the time of day when Leafpool received her vision of the merging trails of stars stretched across the lake. More on that in a bit. Anyway, how's the book itself? As always…it's just terrific! The imagination and passion that the authors spin into their tales is clearly on display here. Even when I started to get physically tired I didn't want to stop reading it! One reason I love it is the imagery the authors employ, particularly towards the beginning, where Leafpool goes to the lakeshore because she can't sleep. The vision she receives is exactly like the one depicted on the cover of the first edition. It's just written beautifully and perfectly complements the image! The emotions of course are just as strong as ever and the dilemmas presented feel true to real life despite being about cats living in a semi-fantasy world.<br /><br />Characters: The characters in this book are just as good as ever and I've come to love this next generation of warriors just as much as the previous ones! They simultaneously manage to frustrate, delight, and inspire me all at once. And yet never do the characters do anything that feels out of character for them. Creating memorable and likable yet flawed characters is a hard task for any writer, but these women have both a subtle grasp and rich command of the tales they weave with these cats!<br /><br />Brambleclaw – I can safely say now, having read not just this book but the whole "New Prophecy" arc that Brambleclaw is now probably my second-favorite hero of this series after Firestar. I might even dare say that, as great of a character Firestar is, Brambleclaw has quite a bit more angles to him. For me, at least from what I've read thus far, he's probably one of the most complexly written characters in the series. I really felt his dilemma of wanting to be close to his birth family, even as I wanted him to remember the unenviable legacy he hails from and see his half-brother for who he is. As in "Starlight," I strongly felt his desire to be recognized for all his hard work by becoming deputy of ThunderClan. Yet I also wanted him so badly to face the truth about his quest for power and how much it was starting to parallel his father's. And when he finally did, it was SO cathartic and SO much of a relief after having to read about his struggle for three days straight! That said, I can imagine how tough of a decision it was for him to kill Hawkfrost. Not only was he Brambleclaw's half-brother, but Brambleclaw had only just realized he doesn't want to be a power-hungry tyrant and bloodthirsty killer like his father. But in spite of all that, I'm so glad he's finally on the light side again (to use a "Star Wars" reference) and I see a bright future for him and his career as ThunderClan's new deputy!<br /><br />Leafpool – Given that hers is the only point of view we read through throughout this entire arc, I've always thought of Leafpool as the heart and soul of the "New Prophecy" arc. She's come such a long way from (for lack of a better way to put it) the innocent apprentice she was at the beginning of "Midnight." She's grown in her faith tremendously and has proven herself willing to learn from her mistakes and become all the wiser for it. Yet at the same time, she still has plenty of room to grow even more and go even further as a character. She also perfectly complements her sister Squirrelflight in that they're both passionate about helping and defending the downtrodden, they just do it in different ways. Even so, Leafpool has definitely had to carry more burdens than Squirrelflight, and heavier ones at that. Sure, you could fault her at first for keeping her knowledge of Brambleclaw's dream visits. But she also has to consider both her feelings toward him and her sister's love for him, as well as whether or not it would be safe for her to tell Firestar and ThunderClan about it. Moreover, she has to take on the unprecedented challenge of taking responsibility for half of Willowpaw's training. And even if Cinderpelt's death wasn't her fault, I really felt her guilt and grief. Cinderpelt was like something of a second mother to her. That said, I was glad that Leafpool still found the strength to carry on as the sole medicine cat of ThunderClan.<br /><br />Mothwing – I was honestly kind of surprised at how much I came to love Mothwing's character. I always liked her throughout the "New Prophecy" arc and deeply cared for her struggle. I am a little embarrassed to admit that I was a kinda frustrated with her lack of faith in StarClan and her attempts to explain away Leafpool's dreams, even as she assured Leafpool she didn't believe she was lying. But then I read about how her faith was pretty much destroyed when her brother revealed that he'd planted the false moth's wing sign, and I found it just completely and utterly heartbreaking and even a little violating. And yet that made StarClan's mercy and grace toward her and their faith in her, even if she didn't return that faith, all the more wonderful. She clearly loves and cares for her Clan and it was great to see her finally find the courage to stand up to her bully of a brother!<br /><br />Tigerstar and Hawkfrost – This story couldn't have had a more perfect beginning than showing us Tigerstar's plans for his sons. Even in death, he's still scheming and plotting and willing to do whatever it takes to get revenge on Firestar and remold the Clans as he sees fit. If anything, he's more evil dead (no pun intended) than he was alive, since once one goes to the Dark Forest, there's absolutely no going back to the light side. Not to mention, he's also very much a hypocrite for being a sort of racist against non-Clanborn and half-Clan cats, when he was willing to take in Sasha as a mate and father her kits. That said, Hawkfrost proved to be just as much of a despicable villain as his father! Arguably more so in some ways! When I returned to this series, while I did know that Hawkfrost was kind of Brambleclaw's evil twin in a way, I wasn't prepared for how much of a fox-hearted bully he is! He bullies everyone he dislikes and sees as being in his way, from his half-brother to his sister to his former Clanmate Stormfur! He even goes so far as to mock Brambleclaw's commitment to the warrior code, showing how much of a hypocrite he is – like father, like son, after all – and how he's only willing to follow the code as long as it's convenient.<br /><br />Firestar – He may have been more of a background character in this arc, but I love the spotlight this book gives to Firestar (and how he's on the cover of the version I read). Even though I understood his Clanmates wanting him to appoint a new deputy, I knew just as much as Firestar that Graystripe was still alive. And while I'm now totally supportive of Brambleclaw being the new deputy of ThunderClan, it was still just a massive punch to the feels to see Firestar give in and declare his best friend legally dead in order to appoint Brambleclaw. But what's arguably Firestar's best scene in this entire arc (for me, at least) is when he's entangled in the fox trap, on the verge of losing not just one life but all of his remaining ones, and yet he still believes in Brambleclaw and is willing to put all his lives in his new deputy's paws. It's that scene alone that ultimately convinced Brambleclaw to come back to the light side, and really shows you just how important Firestar is to ThunderClan and Brambleclaw's life.<br /><br />Various Other Characters – Even if Squirrelflight doesn't feature as much here as she did in previous books, she's just as good as ever and I'm so glad that she and Brambleclaw are finally getting back together! That said, I'm still a little nervous about what her reaction will be if she finds out about Brambleclaw's dream visits. I was also intrigued by Ashfur's character. I do feel bad for him in that he obviously loved and cared so much about Squirrelflight, only to end up losing her to not just any other tom, but Brambleclaw. That said, while I do believe he'll continue to be a faithful ThunderClan warrior, I am curious as to how this troubling loss will impact his future as a character. I also thought Willowpaw was adorable and even as precocious as Leafpool was when she was an apprentice. I felt just awful about how Berrykit had to have half his tail amputated. But at the same time, I look forward to his future training under Brambleclaw! And it felt good to see the somewhat adorably oblivious Cloudtail and Brightheart get back together.<br /><br />Overall: This book was just a spectacular conclusion to the "New Prophecy" arc, with pretty much everything I wanted the story to be! As was the case with the "Dawn of the Clans" arc and the "Prophecies Begin" arc, I feel like I've really gotten to see the characters grow and mature throughout this one, and experience their shared journey alongside them. That said, I absolutely cannot wait to start the "Power of Three" arc!</span>
  <a data-text-id="6280357442523376761" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_248111346" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/248111346" />
    <a title="Lindsey" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4564269-lindsey"><img alt="Lindsey" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1296079752p2/4564269.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/248111346?book_show_action=true">Dec 17, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lindsey" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lindsey" href="/user/show/4564269-lindsey">Lindsey</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Warriors fans</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4564269-lindsey?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4564269-lindsey?shelf=series">series</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4564269-lindsey?shelf=animals">animals</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4564269-lindsey?shelf=warriors">warriors</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer248111346" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13016650734744552406">Okay, this was the best Warriors books so far. 4.5 I wish I could give. <br/><br/>It has the edge on Forest of Secrets mostly because I really love the brothers. I still take issue with some of the overly easy characterization the Erins do, which is why I can't give it a five. But the pace was amazing, the intrigue was great and the character arcs were brilliant. I loved this book. It makes me want to jump right into The Power of Three series, even though I've heard that is... not as good. Characters like</span>
  <span id="freeText13016650734744552406" style="display:none">Okay, this was the best Warriors books so far. 4.5 I wish I could give. <br /><br />It has the edge on Forest of Secrets mostly because I really love the brothers. I still take issue with some of the overly easy characterization the Erins do, which is why I can't give it a five. But the pace was amazing, the intrigue was great and the character arcs were brilliant. I loved this book. It makes me want to jump right into The Power of Three series, even though I've heard that is... not as good. Characters like Squirrelflight, Brambleclaw, Mothwing and Leafpool were all worth reading about their development and choices, as well as my old favorites of Cloudtail, Brightheart and Mistyfoot. As I mentioned before, I am also forgiving of Brambleclaw's indecisive attitude regarding his desire for power in that he feels his father's influence, but it is helped by the fact that Brambleclaw does consider things and reevaluate his positions based on the right catalysts. While Squirrelflight's attitude toward Brambleclaw is bizarre because she, nor Leafpool, have any reason to constantly wonder whether Brambleclaw is like his father, I will allow that it is mostly her frustration at his refusal to consider her perspective. I also feel really, really awful for poor Leafpool <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[especially since I know how things turn out for her in The Power of Three <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>.<br /><br />That said, The New Prophecy should have been four books, not six. Dawn was a total waste of time. And much of Starlight could've been handled in Twilight. The overall pacing of the series was atrocious ad the in-between books really dragged. I probably won't be picking up Power of Three for another several months, as I might be kitty'd out, but I hope, for all its other flaws, that it knows how to pace itself.<br /><br />One more thing that was probably my BIGGEST frustration with the final three books. After spending half of the second series trying to convince readers that the Warriors need to learn to make their own decisions and not look to StarClan for everything, the final three books completely throw this idea out the window. Almost EVERY major decision is a result of StarClan interference <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Leafpool deciding to run away with Crowfeather, Leafpool deciding it's all right for her sister to be mates with Brambleclaw, Squirrelflight making the same decision, Firestar deciding to make Brambleclaw deputy, Leafpool figuring out Mothwing's secret... HELL the only cat who makes his own decisions IS Brambleclaw, who makes the climatic decision to save Firestar <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>. THIS IS RIDICULOUS. I don't like the agency it takes from the characters, and I'm particularly disturbed that it suggests to its children readers to look toward someone else when making their decisions, higher power or no. This extensive reliance on StarClan was never present in the original series, and it shouldn't be here. I hope this element is also excised from The Power of Three.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13016650734744552406" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('hEXoyh7Kr5cULVqimLQtCqm8zYmrdkdorV38zGM8yWA3RmmekaPnfRDmSwW2tekXFyY98oKCcTH+nNh+rRFRXQ==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('cwnBsGvYeFXizsEpnwkvHAc/rKYrzyz/Dr8uyCqKsDDACkDk5LEwv+YF0I6xCOsBuaVc3QI7GqZdfgp65KcoDQ==')})
  }

Sutherland</a>, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/2742182.Gillian_Philip" title="Gillian Philip" rel="nofollow noopener">Gillian Philip</a>, and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/769868.Inbali_Iserles" title="Inbali Iserles" rel="nofollow noopener">Inbali Iserles</a>, as well as editor <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/645010.Victoria_Holmes" title="Victoria Holmes" rel="nofollow noopener">Victoria Holmes</a>. Together, they write the Warriors series as well as the Seekers and Survivors series. Erin Hunter is working on a new series now called Bravelands. <br /><br />Erin Hunter is inspired by a love of cats and a fascination with the ferocity of the natural world. As well as having a great respect for nature in all its forms, Erin enjoys creating rich mythical explanations for animal behavior, shaped by her interest in astronomy and standing stones.</span>
